User Benefit: Users can generate personalized responses efficiently, ensure response accuracy, and maintain consistent messaging across communications.

5. Enhanced Consistency: Standardizing responses to common inquiries will ensure consistent messaging and information delivery, reducing the risk of contradictory information being provided to recipients.

Prompt:
Email Routing is a feature that involves defining rules for directing incoming emails to specific folders or recipients based on predefined criteria. In the context of the Email Router system described in the Product Specification Document, the Email Routing feature includes the following components:

1. Rules-Based Engine: The system will have a development of a rules-based engine that can analyze the content of incoming emails to determine the appropriate handling. These rules can be configured based on various criteria such as keywords, sender information, urgency levels, or specific content within the email.

2. Context-Aware Forwarding: The routing logic will include context-aware forwarding, which means that relevant metadata and previous correspondence history will be taken into account when deciding where to route the email. This ensures that the email is directed to the most suitable recipient or folder based on the context of the communication.

3. Assignment to Subject Matter Experts (SMEs): Complex or high-confidence emails will be automatically routed to the appropriate Subject Matter Experts (SMEs) based on the predefined rules. This ensures that specialized inquiries are directed to individuals with the expertise to provide accurate and timely responses.

4. Manual Override Options: The system will also provide manual override options to allow human intervention when necessary. This means that users can intervene in the automated routing process if they believe a different handling is required based on their judgment or specific knowledge of the situation.

By implementing robust email routing rules within the Email Router system, organizations can ensure that incoming emails are efficiently directed to the right recipients or folders, reducing response times, improving communication accuracy, and enhancing overall operational efficiency.

   - Utilize LLM-based classifiers to analyze email content and determine intent and category.

--- Interaction 1 ---
 Step 1: Worker agent generates a response to the prompt
Prompt:
Based on the provided knowledge, the design of the filter creation interface for the Email Router system should align with the product features and functional requirements outlined in the Product Specification Document. Here is a suggested approach for designing the filter creation interface:

1. **Filter Creation Section**: 
   - The interface should have a dedicated section for creating and managing filters.
   - Users should be able to easily access this section from the main dashboard or configuration panel.

2. **Filter Criteria Selection**:
   - Provide options for users to define filter criteria based on email content, sender, recipient, subject, urgency, or any other relevant metadata.
   - Include dropdown menus, text fields, checkboxes, and radio buttons for selecting filter criteria.

3. **Filter Conditions**:
   - Allow users to set conditions for each filter criterion, such as contains, does not contain, equals, does not equal, etc.
   - Users should be able to combine multiple conditions using AND/OR logic to create complex filter rules.

4. **Filter Actions**:
   - Enable users to define actions to be taken when an email matches the filter criteria.
   - Actions may include routing the email to a specific SME, applying a label, marking as high priority, or triggering an automated response.

5. **Filter Testing**:
   - Provide a testing feature that allows users to simulate how the filter would categorize incoming emails based on the defined criteria.
   - Users should be able to preview the results of the filter before saving it.

6. **Filter Management**:
   - Allow users to view, edit, enable, disable, and delete existing filters.
   - Include options for organizing filters into folders or categories for better management.

7. **Save and Apply**:
   - Include a save button to store the created filter for future use.
   - Ensure that users can apply the filter immediately after saving to start routing emails based on the defined criteria.

8. **User-Friendly Interface**:
   - Design the interface with a clean layout, intuitive navigation, and clear instructions to guide users through the filter creation process.
   - Use visual cues such as icons, color-coded elements, and tooltips to enhance usability.

By incorporating these elements into the filter creation interface, users of the Email Router system will be able to efficiently set up and manage filters to automate email routing and improve operational efficiency.
Worker Agent Response:
The design approach for the filter creation interface for the Email Router system aligns well with the product features and functional requirements outlined in the Product Specification Document. By providing users with a dedicated section for creating and managing filters, along with options for defining filter criteria, conditions, actions, testing, and management, the interface ensures that users can effectively automate email routing and enhance operational efficiency. The emphasis on user-friendly design, intuitive navigation, and clear instructions further enhances the usability of the interface, making it easier for users to set up and apply filters to incoming emails.

--- Interaction 1 ---
 Step 1: Worker agent generates a response to the prompt
Prompt:
Development Task: Implement Filter Logic

1. Task Description:
   - Develop filter logic to categorize incoming emails based on predefined rules.
   - Define criteria for filtering emails into different categories such as urgent, routine, sales inquiries, etc.
   - Ensure that the filter logic is configurable to allow for easy adjustments based on changing requirements.
   - Test the filter logic to verify accurate categorization of emails according to the defined rules.

2. Subtasks:
   a. Define filter criteria:
      - Identify key attributes for categorizing emails (e.g., keywords, sender, subject line, urgency).
      - Determine the rules for each category (e.g., if email contains "urgent" in subject, categorize as high priority).

   b. Develop filter logic:
      - Implement algorithms to evaluate incoming emails against the defined criteria.
      - Create a decision-making process to assign emails to appropriate categories based on the filter rules.

   c. Configurability:
      - Design a user-friendly interface for administrators to modify filter rules easily.
      - Ensure that changes to filter criteria can be applied without requiring code changes.

   d. Testing:
      - Conduct unit tests to validate the accuracy of email categorization.
      - Perform integration testing to ensure seamless integration with the existing email routing system.
      - Run end-to-end tests to simulate real-world scenarios and verify the effectiveness of the filter logic.

3. Deliverables:
   - Filter logic module with defined criteria and rules.
   - Configurable interface for managing filter criteria.
   - Test reports demonstrating the accuracy and effectiveness of the implemented filter logic.

4. Timeline:
   - Task Duration: 2 weeks
   - Start Date: [To be determined]
   - End Date: [To be determined]

5. Dependencies:
   - Availability of email data for testing purposes.
   - Collaboration with the email routing system development team for integration.

6. Risks:
   - Inaccurate categorization leading to misrouted emails.
   - Difficulty in defining clear and effective filter criteria.
   - Integration challenges with the existing email infrastructure.

7. Notes:
   - Regular communication with stakeholders to gather feedback on filter logic performance.

Worker Agent Response:
Product: Email Router System

1. Email Ingestion System
   - **Purpose**: Seamless integration with email services via SMTP, IMAP, and RESTful APIs to retrieve incoming messages in real-time.
   - **Key Functionality**: Real-time email retrieval and preprocessing to extract relevant metadata and content.
   - **User Benefits**: Users can receive and process incoming emails efficiently without delays, ensuring timely responses to customer inquiries.

2. Message Classification Module
   - **Purpose**: Utilization of LLM-based classifiers to analyze email content and determine intent and category.
   - **Key Functionality**: Assigns confidence scores to decide between automated responses and manual handling.
   - **User Benefits**: Ensures accurate classification of emails, enabling the system to prioritize and handle messages effectively based on their content.

3. Knowledge Base Integration
   - **Purpose**: Implementation of a vector database for efficient storage and retrieval of organizational knowledge.
   - **Key Functionality**: Continuous learning mechanism to update the knowledge base with new information from resolved inquiries.
   - **User Benefits**: Provides quick access to relevant information for generating responses, improving response accuracy and consistency.

4. Response Generation Engine
   - **Purpose**: Deployment of a RAG system to generate contextually accurate and human-like responses.
   - **Key Functionality**: Incorporation of an approval workflow for reviewing and editing automated responses before dispatch.
   - **User Benefits**: Enables the system to generate personalized responses for routine inquiries, saving time for staff and ensuring consistent messaging.

5. Routing Logic
   - **Purpose**: Development of a rules-based engine to assign emails to appropriate SMEs based on content analysis.
   - **Key Functionality**: Context-aware forwarding that includes relevant metadata and previous correspondence history.
   - **User Benefits**: Ensures that complex inquiries are directed to the right experts, improving response accuracy and efficiency.

6. User Interface
   - **Purpose**: Creation of a comprehensive dashboard for monitoring system performance and metrics.
   - **Key Functionality**: Provision of a configuration panel for managing the knowledge base, routing rules, and system settings.
   - **User Benefits**: Allows users to track system performance, response times, and accuracy easily, facilitating efficient management and optimization of email handling processes.

7. Manual Intervention Options
   - **Purpose**: Implementation of manual override options to allow human intervention when necessary.
   - **Key Functionality**: Enables users to adjust filter rules manually and intervene in the automated process.
   - **User Benefits**: Provides flexibility and control to users, ensuring that they can make necessary adjustments to email handling based on specific requirements or exceptions.

--- Interaction 1 ---
 Step 1: Worker agent generates a response to the prompt
Prompt:
**Feature:** Email Routing Rule Configuration

**Description:**
This feature allows administrators to set up email routing rules for different user groups within the organization. By defining specific criteria and conditions, administrators can ensure that incoming emails are automatically directed to the appropriate subject matter experts (SMEs) based on the nature of the inquiry.

**User Stories:**
1. As an administrator, I want to define routing rules based on keywords or phrases in the email content to ensure that inquiries related to specific topics are routed to the relevant SMEs.
   
2. As an administrator, I want to establish routing rules based on the sender's email address or domain to direct messages from certain contacts to designated SMEs.
   
3. As an administrator, I want to create routing rules based on the urgency or priority level indicated in the email subject line to ensure timely responses to critical inquiries.
   
4. As an administrator, I want to configure routing rules that consider the time of day or day of the week to manage email distribution during different operational hours.
   
5. As an administrator, I want to set up routing rules that prioritize emails from VIP clients or specific stakeholders to guarantee prompt and personalized attention.

**Acceptance Criteria:**
1. The system should allow administrators to create, edit, and delete routing rules through a user-friendly interface.
   
2. Routing rules should support a variety of conditions such as keywords, sender information, urgency levels, and time-based criteria.
   
3. Administrators should be able to prioritize and sequence routing rules to ensure that emails are processed in the desired order.
   
4. Changes to routing rules should be reflected in real-time without requiring system restarts or manual interventions.
   
5. The system should log all routing rule modifications for audit purposes and provide a history of changes made by administrators.
Worker Agent Response:

It allows administrators to define specific criteria and conditions for routing incoming emails to the appropriate subject matter experts (SMEs) within the organization. Here are the user stories and acceptance criteria for this feature:

**User Stories:**

4. As an administrator, I want to configure routing rules that consider the time of day or day of the week to manage email distribution during different operational hours.
   
5. As an administrator, I want to set up routing rules that prioritize emails from VIP clients or specific stakeholders to guarantee prompt and personalized attention.

**Acceptance Criteria:**
1. The system should allow administrators to create, edit, and delete routing rules through a user-friendly interface.
   
2. Routing rules should support a variety of conditions such as keywords, sender information, urgency levels, and time-based criteria.
   
3. Administrators should be able to prioritize and sequence routing rules to ensure that emails are processed in the desired order.
   
4. Changes to routing rules should be reflected in real-time without requiring system restarts or manual interventions.

Prompt:
The routing rule structure in the Email Router system is designed to automatically assign incoming emails to the appropriate subject matter experts (SMEs) based on the content analysis and predefined business rules. The routing rule structure includes the following components:

1. Content Analysis: The system analyzes the content of incoming emails using natural language processing to determine the intent, urgency, and required expertise needed to address the inquiry.

2. Rule-Based Engine: A rules-based engine is developed to define criteria for routing emails to specific SMEs. These rules can be based on keywords, phrases, sender information, email content, or any other relevant factors.

3. Context-Aware Forwarding: The routing logic includes context-aware forwarding, which takes into consideration relevant metadata and previous correspondence history when assigning emails to SMEs. This ensures that the SMEs have the necessary context to provide accurate and timely responses.

4. Confidence Scores: The system assigns confidence scores to each email classification to guide the routing process. Emails with high confidence scores indicating complex or specialized inquiries are routed to SMEs, while those with lower scores may be handled through automated responses.

5. Manual Override: The routing rule structure also includes provisions for manual intervention, allowing human users to override automated routing decisions when necessary. This ensures flexibility and the ability to handle exceptions or unique situations that may not fit the predefined rules.

Overall, the routing rule structure in the Email Router system aims to streamline the email triage process, ensure that emails are directed to the most appropriate recipients, and facilitate timely and accurate responses to incoming inquiries.
Worker Agent Response:
The routing rule structure in the Email Router system is designed to automate the assignment of incoming emails to the correct subject matter experts (SMEs) based on content analysis and predefined business rules. It consists of several key components:

1. **Content Analysis:** The system uses natural language processing to analyze the content of incoming emails, determining intent, urgency, and required expertise.

2. **Rule-Based Engine:** A rules-based engine is implemented to establish criteria for routing emails to specific SMEs. These rules can be based on keywords, sender information, or email content.

3. **Context-Aware Forwarding:** The routing logic considers relevant metadata and previous correspondence history when assigning emails to SMEs, ensuring they have the necessary context for accurate responses.

4. **Confidence Scores:** Each email classification is assigned a confidence score to guide the routing process. Emails with high scores for complex inquiries are routed to SMEs, while lower-scoring emails may be handled automatically.

5. **Manual Override:** The system allows for manual intervention, enabling users to override automated routing decisions when needed. This flexibility accommodates exceptions or unique situations.

Overall, the routing rule structure aims to streamline email triage, ensure emails reach the right recipients, and facilitate prompt and accurate responses to inquiries.

 Step 1: Worker agent generates a response to the prompt
Prompt:
Based on the provided product specification, the development of a routing rule management interface is a crucial feature for the Email Router system. This interface will allow users to define and manage rules for routing emails to the appropriate subject matter experts based on content analysis. Here are the key components and functionalities that should be included in the routing rule management interface:

1. Rule Creation:
   - Users should be able to create new routing rules based on various criteria such as keywords, sender information, email content, or other metadata.
   - The interface should provide options for users to define conditions that trigger the routing of emails to specific subject matter experts.

2. Rule Editing:
   - Users should have the ability to edit existing routing rules to modify conditions, actions, or priorities.
   - The interface should allow for the adjustment of rule parameters based on feedback and system performance.

3. Rule Prioritization:
   - The interface should support the prioritization of routing rules to ensure that emails are directed to the most appropriate subject matter experts in case of conflicting rules.

4. Rule Testing:
   - Users should be able to test routing rules to simulate how emails would be routed based on different scenarios.
   - The interface should provide feedback on the expected outcomes of the routing rules to help users validate their configurations.

5. Rule Monitoring:
   - The interface should include monitoring capabilities to track the performance of routing rules, including the number of emails routed, accuracy rates, and any issues encountered.
   - Users should be able to view analytics related to the effectiveness of each routing rule in directing emails to the right recipients.

6. Rule Deactivation:
   - Users should have the option to deactivate or temporarily disable routing rules that are no longer relevant or causing unintended consequences.
   - The interface should allow for easy reactivation of deactivated rules when needed.

7. User Permissions:
   - The interface should incorporate role-based access control to restrict access to rule management functionalities based on user roles.
   - Administrative users should have the authority to manage routing rules, while other users may have view-only permissions.

By implementing a comprehensive routing rule management interface with these features, users will be able to efficiently configure and optimize the email routing process within the Email Router system, leading to improved accuracy, efficiency, and consistency in handling incoming communications.

2. **Configure Routing Rules**: Set up the routing rules in the system based on the defined scenarios. Ensure that the rules are accurately configured to match the criteria for routing emails to the correct SMEs.

3. **Generate Test Emails**: Create test emails that align with the defined scenarios. These emails should contain content that triggers the routing rules you have set up.

4. **Send Test Emails**: Send the test emails to the designated email addresses that the Email Router system is monitoring. Make sure to send each test email individually to observe how the system handles them one by one.

5. **Monitor Routing Decisions**: Monitor the system's behavior as it receives and processes the test emails. Verify that the routing decisions align with the configured rules and that emails are being directed to the appropriate SMEs accurately.

Prompt:
To implement a notification system for the Email Router project, the following development tasks need to be defined:

1. **Requirement Analysis**:
   - Define the purpose of notifications (e.g., system alerts, response status updates, performance metrics).
   - Identify the types of notifications needed (e.g., email arrival alerts, response completion notifications, system error alerts).

2. **Notification Design**:
   - Determine the format of notifications (e.g., email alerts, in-app notifications, SMS alerts).
   - Design the notification content to be informative and actionable for users.
   - Define the frequency of notifications (e.g., real-time, daily summaries).

3. **Notification Trigger Logic**:
   - Identify the events that will trigger notifications (e.g., new email arrival, response generation, routing to SME).
   - Define the conditions under which notifications should be sent (e.g., urgency level, response time threshold).

4. **Notification Delivery**:
   - Implement the mechanism for sending notifications (e.g., email APIs, push notifications).
   - Ensure notifications are delivered securely and reliably.
   - Consider integrating with existing communication channels for seamless delivery.

5. **User Preferences**:
   - Allow users to customize their notification settings (e.g., frequency, preferred channels).
   - Provide options for users to opt-in or opt-out of specific types of notifications.

6. **Notification Tracking**:
   - Implement logging mechanisms to track when notifications are sent and received.
   - Monitor the effectiveness of notifications in improving system awareness and user engagement.

7. **Testing and Validation**:
   - Conduct thorough testing to ensure notifications are triggered accurately and delivered promptly.
   - Validate that users receive notifications as expected and that the content is clear and actionable.

8. **Documentation**:
   - Document the notification system architecture, including trigger events, delivery mechanisms, and user preferences.
   - Provide user guides on how to set up and manage notification preferences.

By defining and implementing these development tasks, the Email Router project can successfully integrate a notification system to keep users informed about important events and updates within the system.

--- Interaction 1 ---
 Step 1: Worker agent generates a response to the prompt
Prompt:
Notification triggers can be a valuable feature to enhance the Email Router system. By integrating notification triggers, the system can automatically alert users or administrators based on specific events or conditions within the email management process. These triggers can help improve communication efficiency, ensure timely responses, and provide visibility into critical system activities.

Here is how the integration of notification triggers can be implemented within the Email Router system:

1. Define Trigger Events: Identify key events or conditions that warrant notifications, such as the arrival of high-priority emails, completion of automated responses, escalation of inquiries to SMEs, or system performance issues.

2. Configure Trigger Rules: Establish rules that determine when notifications should be triggered, including criteria like email urgency, response time thresholds, knowledge base updates, or system errors.

3. Notification Channels: Define the channels through which notifications will be delivered, such as email alerts, SMS messages, in-app notifications, or integration with collaboration tools like Slack or Microsoft Teams.

4. Customization Options: Provide users with the ability to customize notification preferences based on their roles, responsibilities, and preferences. Allow for setting notification frequency, content, and recipients.

5. Real-time Monitoring: Ensure that notifications are triggered in real-time to enable prompt actions and responses. Monitor system performance to minimize delays in notification delivery.

6. Logging and Audit Trail: Maintain a log of all triggered notifications for tracking and auditing purposes. Include details such as the triggering event, timestamp, recipient, and action taken.

By integrating notification triggers into the Email Router system, users can stay informed about critical email management activities, respond promptly to urgent inquiries, and proactively address system issues. This feature can contribute to enhancing operational efficiency, improving communication quality, and supporting the achievement of the system's objectives.
Worker Agent Response:
The integration of notification triggers into the Email Router system can indeed be a valuable feature to enhance communication efficiency and ensure timely responses. By defining trigger events, configuring trigger rules, determining notification channels, providing customization options, enabling real-time monitoring, and maintaining a logging and audit trail, users can benefit from improved visibility and proactive management of critical system activities. This feature aligns with the system's objectives of reducing response times, increasing efficiency, improving routing accuracy, enhancing consistency, and liberating staff resources. It can contribute to operational excellence by keeping users informed and enabling prompt actions in response to key events within the email management process.

3. **Knowledge Base Management**: The interface should provide options for managing the knowledge base. Users should be able to add, edit, or remove information from the knowledge base, ensuring that it stays up to date with the latest resolved inquiries.

4. **Routing Rules Configuration**: Users should have the ability to define and modify routing rules based on content analysis. This includes setting criteria for automatically assigning emails to appropriate subject matter experts.

6. **System Settings**: Users should be able to adjust general system settings such as notification preferences, language preferences, and other customization options to tailor the system to their specific needs.

 Step 1: Worker agent generates a response to the prompt
Prompt:
Development Plan for Email Router System

1. Define User Stories:
- Identify user stories based on functional requirements such as email ingestion, message classification, knowledge base retrieval, response generation, email routing, and user interface.
- User stories should focus on the actions users can perform with the system and the value they derive from each feature.

2. Breakdown User Stories into Development Tasks:
- For each user story, break down the tasks required to implement the feature.
- Tasks may include coding specific modules, integrating APIs, setting up databases, creating UI components, and testing functionalities.

3. Prioritize Development Tasks:
- Prioritize tasks based on dependencies, criticality to system functionality, and impact on achieving project objectives.
- Ensure that tasks related to core functionalities like email ingestion and message classification are prioritized early in the development process.

4. Assign Tasks to Development Team Members:
- Assign tasks to developers based on their expertise and workload capacity.
- Ensure that each team member understands their responsibilities and timelines for task completion.

Prompt:
To create a comprehensive project plan for the Email Router product, you can start by defining user stories based on the product specification. Each user story should represent a specific functionality or feature that the system needs to deliver. Here are some examples of user stories for the Email Router product:

1. As a customer support representative, I want incoming emails to be automatically categorized based on their content so that I can focus on addressing complex issues rather than routine inquiries.

2. As an IT administrator, I want the system to seamlessly integrate with our existing email infrastructure via SMTP, IMAP, and RESTful APIs to ensure smooth operation and data flow.

3. As a subject matter expert, I want to receive only relevant and complex inquiries routed to me based on the content analysis to improve efficiency and response accuracy.

4. As a system administrator, I want to monitor system performance through a comprehensive dashboard displaying key metrics such as response times and accuracy to ensure optimal operation.

Once you have defined user stories, you can identify key features and functionalities that need to be developed to fulfill each user story. For example, key features for the user story "As a customer support representative, I want incoming emails to be automatically categorized based on their content" may include:

- Email Ingestion System: Develop a module to retrieve incoming emails in real-time and extract relevant metadata.
- Message Classification Module: Implement LLM-based classifiers to analyze email content and determine intent and category.
- Knowledge Base Integration: Create a database for storing organizational knowledge and updating it with new information from resolved inquiries.

After identifying key features, you can break them down into specific development tasks. For instance, for the feature "Email Ingestion System," development tasks may include:

- Set up connections to designated email services using SMTP, IMAP, and RESTful APIs.
- Develop algorithms to preprocess emails and extract metadata such as sender, recipient, subject, and timestamp.
- Implement real-time email retrieval mechanisms to ensure timely processing of incoming messages.

By following this approach and breaking down user stories into key features and development tasks, you can create a detailed project plan for the Email Router product that outlines the development work required to meet the specified objectives and requirements.

Email Ingestion System
Description: This feature allows seamless integration with email services via SMTP, IMAP, and RESTful APIs.
Key Functionality: Real-time email retrieval and preprocessing to extract relevant metadata and content.
User Benefit: Users can efficiently connect to designated email services, retrieve incoming messages in real-time, and extract essential information from emails without delays.

Message Classification Module
Description: This feature utilizes LLM-based classifiers to analyze email content and determine intent and category.
Key Functionality: Assigns confidence scores to decide between automated responses and manual handling.
User Benefit: Users can accurately categorize incoming emails, prioritize responses, and ensure efficient handling based on content analysis.

Knowledge Base Integration
Description: This feature implements a vector database for efficient storage and retrieval of organizational knowledge.
Key Functionality: Continuous learning mechanism to update the knowledge base with new information from resolved inquiries.
User Benefit: Users can access relevant organizational knowledge quickly, stay updated with new information, and provide accurate responses to inquiries.

Response Generation Engine
Description: This feature deploys a RAG system to generate contextually accurate and human-like responses.
Key Functionality: Incorporates an approval workflow for reviewing and editing automated responses before dispatch.
User Benefit: Users can generate personalized responses efficiently, ensure response accuracy, and maintain consistent messaging across communications.

Routing Logic
Description: This feature develops a rules-based engine to assign emails to appropriate SMEs based on content analysis.
Key Functionality: Context-aware forwarding that includes relevant metadata and previous correspondence history.
User Benefit: Users can streamline email routing, ensure inquiries reach the right experts promptly, and maintain effective communication flow within the organization.

User Interface
Description: This feature creates a comprehensive dashboard for monitoring system performance, including metrics on response times and accuracy.
Key Functionality: Provides a configuration panel for managing the knowledge base, routing rules, and system settings.
User Benefit: Users can track system performance, make informed decisions based on metrics, and customize system settings for optimal efficiency.

   - **User Benefit:** Helps in accurately categorizing emails and deciding on appropriate responses, improving response quality and efficiency.

   - **Description:** This feature involves the implementation of a vector database for efficient storage and retrieval of organizational knowledge. It includes a continuous learning mechanism to update the knowledge base with new information from resolved inquiries.

   - **Description:** This feature deploys a RAG system to generate contextually accurate and human-like responses. It also includes an approval workflow for reviewing and editing automated responses before dispatch.
   - **Key Functionality:** Contextual response generation, approval workflow.
   - **User Benefit:** Enables the system to generate accurate responses and allows for human oversight to maintain response quality.

   - **Description:** This feature involves the development of a rules-based engine to assign emails to appropriate SMEs based on content analysis. It includes context-aware forwarding that incorporates relevant metadata and previous correspondence history.
   - **Key Functionality:** Rules-based email assignment, context-aware forwarding.

--- Completed Step 6 ---
Based on the information provided in the Product Specification Document, the Email Routing feature in the Email Router system includes the following components:

1. Rules-Based Engine: The system will have a rules-based engine that can analyze incoming emails to determine the appropriate handling based on predefined criteria such as keywords, sender information, urgency levels, or specific content within the email.

2. Context-Aware Forwarding: The routing logic will consider relevant metadata and previous correspondence history when deciding where to route the email. This ensures that emails are directed to the most suitable recipient or folder based on the context of the communication.

3. Assignment to Subject Matter Experts (SMEs): Complex or high-confidence emails will be automatically routed to the appropriate Subject Matter Experts (SMEs) based on predefined rules. This ensures that specialized inquiries are directed to individuals with the expertise to provide accurate responses.

4. Manual Override Options: The system will provide manual override options to allow human intervention when necessary. Users can intervene in the automated routing process if they believe a different handling is required based on their judgment or specific knowledge of the situation.

By incorporating these components into the Email Routing feature of the Email Router system, organizations can streamline email management processes, improve response times, enhance communication accuracy, and increase operational efficiency.

Based on the provided product specification, the feature of "Email Filtering" can be further detailed as follows:

Feature: Email Filtering
Description: The Email Filtering feature enables the system to categorize and prioritize incoming emails based on predefined criteria, such as urgency, topic, or sender, to streamline the email triage process.
Functionalities:
1. Categorization: Automatically categorize incoming emails into predefined categories (e.g., urgent, general inquiries, feedback) using machine learning models.
2. Prioritization: Assign priority levels to emails based on factors like sender importance, keywords, or historical interactions to ensure timely responses to critical messages.
3. Routing Rules: Implement customizable routing rules to direct emails to the appropriate department or individual based on the identified category or priority level.
4. Filtering Criteria: Allow users to set up personalized filtering criteria to flag or route emails that meet specific conditions, enhancing efficiency in handling incoming messages.
5. Dashboard Insights: Provide visual representations on the dashboard of email traffic patterns, categorized emails, and prioritized messages to give users visibility into the email flow.
6. Performance Metrics: Track and display metrics related to email filtering effectiveness, such as accuracy in categorization, response time based on priority, and overall email handling efficiency.
7. User Configuration: Enable users to adjust filtering settings, add new categories, modify prioritization rules, and fine-tune the filtering algorithms to align with organizational needs.
8. Integration: Ensure seamless integration with the existing email infrastructure to capture, filter, and route emails without disrupting the current workflow.
9. Compliance: Adhere to data privacy regulations by handling sensitive information appropriately during the filtering process and ensuring secure handling of emails.
10. Scalability: Design the Email Filtering feature to accommodate increasing email volumes as the organization grows, maintaining performance and accuracy in email categorization and prioritization.

By incorporating the Email Filtering feature into the Email Router system, organizations can effectively manage incoming email communications, reduce response times, and enhance operational efficiency by automating the categorization and prioritization of emails.

1. **Filter Creation Section**:
   - **Description**: This feature provides a dedicated section within the interface for users to create and manage filters.
   - **Key Functionalities**: Users can easily access the filter creation section from the main dashboard or configuration panel.
   - **User Benefits**: Enables users to efficiently set up and organize filters for automating email routing.

2. **Filter Criteria Selection**:
   - **Description**: Users can define filter criteria based on email content, sender, recipient, subject, urgency, or other relevant metadata.
   - **Key Functionalities**: Includes dropdown menus, text fields, checkboxes, and radio buttons for selecting filter criteria.
   - **User Benefits**: Allows users to customize filter criteria to match specific email routing requirements.

3. **Filter Conditions**:
   - **Description**: Users can set conditions for each filter criterion, such as contains, does not contain, equals, does not equal, etc.
   - **Key Functionalities**: Users can combine multiple conditions using AND/OR logic to create complex filter rules.
   - **User Benefits**: Enables users to create precise and tailored filter conditions for accurate email categorization.

4. **Filter Actions**:
   - **Description**: Users can define actions to be taken when an email matches the filter criteria.
   - **Key Functionalities**: Actions may include routing the email to a specific SME, applying a label, marking as high priority, or triggering an automated response.
   - **User Benefits**: Allows users to automate email handling based on predefined criteria, improving operational efficiency.

5. **Filter Testing**:
   - **Description**: Users can simulate how the filter would categorize incoming emails based on the defined criteria.
   - **Key Functionalities**: Provides a preview of the results of the filter before saving it.
   - **User Benefits**: Enables users to validate and fine-tune filter settings before implementation, ensuring accurate email routing.

6. **Filter Management**:
   - **Description**: Users can view, edit, enable, disable, and delete existing filters.
   - **Key Functionalities**: Options for organizing filters into folders or categories for better management.
   - **User Benefits**: Facilitates efficient management of filters, allowing users to maintain and optimize email routing configurations.

7. **Save and Apply**:
   - **Description**: Includes a save button to store the created filter for future use.
   - **Key Functionalities**: Users can apply the filter immediately after saving to start routing emails based on the defined criteria.
   - **User Benefits**: Streamlines the process of saving and applying filters, ensuring seamless implementation of email routing rules.

8. **User-Friendly Interface**:
   - **Description**: The interface is designed with a clean layout, intuitive navigation, and clear instructions to guide users through the filter creation process.
   - **Key Functionalities**: Visual cues such as icons, color-coded elements, and tooltips enhance usability.
   - **User Benefits**: Enhances user experience by making filter creation intuitive and straightforward, improving overall usability and efficiency.

**Key Functionality:**

- Define rules based on keywords or phrases in the email content to route inquiries related to specific topics to relevant SMEs.
- Establish rules based on the sender's email address or domain to direct messages from specific contacts to designated SMEs.
- Set up rules based on urgency or priority levels indicated in the email subject line for timely responses to critical inquiries.
- Configure rules considering the time of day or day of the week to manage email distribution during different operational hours.
- Prioritize and sequence routing rules to ensure emails are processed in the desired order.

**User Benefit:**
The Email Routing Rule Configuration feature streamlines the email management process by automating the routing of incoming emails to the right recipients based on predefined criteria. This improves operational efficiency, ensures timely responses to critical inquiries, and enhances overall communication quality within the organization. Administrators can optimize email handling, reduce manual intervention, and provide personalized attention to VIP clients and stakeholders, ultimately enhancing the user experience and organizational productivity.

   - Feature Name: Intent Analysis
     - Description: Utilization of LLM-based classifiers to analyze email content and determine intent and category.
     - Key Functionality: Assigning confidence scores to guide automated responses or manual handling decisions.
     - User Benefit: Ensures accurate categorization of emails, leading to timely and appropriate responses.

3. Knowledge Base Integration:
   - Feature Name: Efficient Data Storage
     - Description: Implementation of a vector database for storing and retrieving organizational knowledge effectively.
     - Key Functionality: Continuous learning mechanism to update the knowledge base with new information.
     - User Benefit: Enables quick access to relevant information and ensures knowledge base remains up-to-date.

4. Response Generation Engine:
   - Feature Name: Contextual Response Generation
     - Description: Deployment of a RAG system to generate contextually accurate and human-like responses.
     - Key Functionality: Incorporation of an approval workflow for reviewing and editing automated responses.
     - User Benefit: Provides users with accurate and personalized responses, enhancing communication quality.

5. Routing Logic:
   - Feature Name: Efficient Email Routing
     - Description: Development of rules-based engine for assigning emails to appropriate SMEs.
     - Key Functionality: Context-aware forwarding with relevant metadata and correspondence history.
     - User Benefit: Ensures emails are directed to the right experts promptly, improving response times.

6. User Interface:
   - Feature Name: Comprehensive Dashboard
     - Description: Creation of a dashboard for monitoring system performance and key metrics.
     - Key Functionality: Provision of a configuration panel for managing knowledge base and routing rules.
     - User Benefit: Allows users to track system performance, manage settings, and intervene manually when needed.
